The 2011 <a href="/wiki/Honda_CR-Z" title="Honda CR-Z">Honda CR-Z</a> hybrid was launched in Japan in February 2010, followed by the US in August 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-GCC0210_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0210-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Auris_HSD_Hybrid_Concept.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Toyota_Auris_HSD_Hybrid_Concept.JPG/220px-Toyota_Auris_HSD_Hybrid_Concept.JPG" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Toyota_Auris_HSD_Hybrid_Concept.JPG/330px-Toyota_Auris_HSD_Hybrid_Concept.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Toyota_Auris_HSD_Hybrid_Concept.JPG/440px-Toyota_Auris_HSD_Hybrid_Concept.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Auris_HSD_Hybrid_Concept.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The 2011 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Auris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Auris Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Auris Hybrid</a> is the first <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">mass-produced</a> hybrid electric vehicle built in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-JustA_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JustA-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dt>2009–2010</dt>
</dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Elantra_LPI_Hybrid" title="Hyundai Elantra LPI Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Hyundai Elantra LPI Hybrid</a> was unveiled at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Motor_Show" title="Seoul Motor Show">Seoul Motor Show</a>, and sales began in the <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korean</a> domestic market in July 2009. The Elantra LPI (Liquefied Petroleum Injected) is the world's first hybrid vehicle to be powered by an internal combustion engine built to run on <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas" title="Liquefied petroleum gas">liquefied petroleum gas</a> (LPG) as a fuel. The Elantra PLI is a <a href="/wiki/Mild_hybrid" title="Mild hybrid">mild hybrid</a> and the first hybrid to adopt advanced <a href="/wiki/Lithium_polymer" title="Lithium polymer" class="mw-redirect">lithium polymer</a> (Li–Poly) batteries.<sup id="cite_ref-Hyundai0709_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hyundai0709-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The Elantra LPI Hybrid delivers a <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel economy rating</a> of 41.9&#160;miles per US gallon (5.61&#160;L/100&#160;km; 50.3&#160;mpg<sub><small>-imp</small></sub>) and CO<sub>2</sub> emissions of 99 g/km to qualify as a <a href="/wiki/Super_Ultra_Low_Emission_Vehicle" title="Super Ultra Low Emission Vehicle" class="mw-redirect">Super Ultra Low Emission Vehicle</a> (SULEV).<sup id="cite_ref-Hyundai0709_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hyundai0709-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_W221#S_400_Hybrid_.282009-.29" title="Mercedes-Benz W221">Mercedes-Benz S400 BlueHybrid</a> was unveiled in the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Auto_Show" title="Chicago Auto Show">Chicago Auto Show</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gab0209_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gab0209-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> and sales began in the U.S. in October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1009_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1009-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The S400 BlueHybrid is a <a href="/wiki/Mild_hybrid" title="Mild hybrid">mild hybrid</a> and the first hybrid car to adopt a <a href="/wiki/Lithium_ion_battery" title="Lithium ion battery" class="mw-redirect">lithium ion battery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gab0209_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gab0209-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GCC0609_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0609-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The hybrid technology in the S400 was co-developed by <a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler AG</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenMild_23-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenMild-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gab0209_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gab0209-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The same hybrid technology is being used in the <a href="/wiki/BMW_7_Series#ActiveHybrid_7" title="BMW 7 Series">BMW ActiveHybrid 7</a>, expected to go on sales in the U.S. and Europe by mid-2010.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2009 BMW began sales of its full hybrid <a href="/wiki/BMW_X6#ActiveHybrid_X6_.282009.E2.80.93.29" title="BMW X6">BMW ActiveHybrid X6</a>, while Daimler launched the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_M-Class#ML450_Hybrid" title="Mercedes-Benz M-Class">Mercedes-Benz ML450 Hybrid</a> by lease only.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1209_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1209-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sales of the <a href="/wiki/Honda_CR-Z" title="Honda CR-Z">Honda CR-Z</a> began in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> in February 2010, followed by the U.S. and European markets later in the year, becoming Honda's third hybrid electric car in the market.<sup id="cite_ref-GCC0210_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0210-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT0810_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0810-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Honda also launched the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Honda_Fit_Hybrid" title="Honda Fit Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Honda Fit Hybrid</a> in Japan in October 2010, and unveiled the European version, the Honda Jazz Hybrid, at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Paris_Motor_Show" title="2010 Paris Motor Show">2010 Paris Motor Show</a>, which went on sale in some European markets by early 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-GCC100810_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC100810-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">Mass production</a> of the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Auris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Auris Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Auris Hybrid</a> began in May 2010 at Toyota Manufacturing UK (TMUK) <a href="/wiki/Burnaston" title="Burnaston">Burnaston</a> plant and became the first mass-produced hybrid vehicle to be built in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-JustA_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JustA-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Sales in the UK began in July 2010, at a price starting at<span class="nowrap">GB£18,950</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$27,450</span>), <span class="nowrap">GB£550</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$800</span>) less than the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Edmunds1_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edmunds1-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2011 Auris Hybrid shares the same <a href="/wiki/Powertrain" title="Powertrain">powertrain</a> as the Prius, and combined fuel economy is 74.3&#160;mpg<sub><small>-imp</small></sub> (3.80&#160;L/100&#160;km; 61.9&#160;mpg<sub><small>-US</small></sub>).<sup id="cite_ref-AurisH_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AurisH-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 2011 <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKZ_Hybrid" title="Lincoln MKZ Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Lincoln MKZ Hybrid</a> was unveiled at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/New_York_International_Auto_Show" title="New York International Auto Show">New York International Auto Show</a><sup id="cite_ref-GCC0310_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0310-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> and sales began in the U.S. in September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The MKZ Hybrid is the first hybrid version ever to have the same price as the gasoline-engine version of the same car.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Cayenne#Hybrid" title="Porsche Cayenne">Porshe Cayenne Hybrid</a> was launched in the U.S in late 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2010_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2010-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>2011–2013</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VW_Jetta_Hybrid_with_badge_WAS_2012_0711.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/VW_Jetta_Hybrid_with_badge_WAS_2012_0711.jpg/220px-VW_Jetta_Hybrid_with_badge_WAS_2012_0711.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/VW_Jetta_Hybrid_with_badge_WAS_2012_0711.jpg/330px-VW_Jetta_Hybrid_with_badge_WAS_2012_0711.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/VW_Jetta_Hybrid_with_badge_WAS_2012_0711.jpg/440px-VW_Jetta_Hybrid_with_badge_WAS_2012_0711.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VW_Jetta_Hybrid_with_badge_WAS_2012_0711.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
2013 <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Jetta_Hybrid" title="Volkswagen Jetta Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Volkswagen Jetta Hybrid</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> announced at the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show#010" title="Geneva Motor Show">2010 Geneva Motor Show</a> the launch of the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Touareg#Touareg_V6_TSI_Hybrid_.282009.29" title="Volkswagen Touareg">Touareg Hybrid</a>, which went on sale on the U.S. in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> VW also announced plans to introduce <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel</a>-electric hybrid versions of its most popular models in 2012, beginning with the new <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Jetta" title="Volkswagen Jetta">Jetta</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">Golf Hybrid</a> in 2013 together with hybrid versions of the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Polo" title="Volkswagen Polo">Passat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Parkers_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parkers-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AECs_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AECs-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Other gasoline-electric hybrids released in the U.S. in 2011 are the <a href="/wiki/Lexus_CT_200h" title="Lexus CT 200h" class="mw-redirect">Lexus CT 200h</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Infiniti_M35_Hybrid" title="Infiniti M35 Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Infiniti M35 Hybrid</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Sonata_Hybrid" title="Hyundai Sonata Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Hyundai Sonata Hybrid</a> and its siblling the <a href="/wiki/Kia_Optima_Hybrid" title="Kia Optima Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Kia Optima Hybrid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT0410_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0410-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prius_c_WAS_2012_0646.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Prius_c_WAS_2012_0646.JPG/220px-Prius_c_WAS_2012_0646.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Prius_c_WAS_2012_0646.JPG/330px-Prius_c_WAS_2012_0646.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Prius_c_WAS_2012_0646.JPG/440px-Prius_c_WAS_2012_0646.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prius_c_WAS_2012_0646.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The 2012 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_c" title="Toyota Prius c">Toyota Prius c</a> was released in the U.S. in March 2012, and was launched in Japan as Toyota Aqua in December 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_3008_HYbrid4" title="Peugeot 3008 HYbrid4" class="mw-redirect">Peugeot 3008 HYbrid4</a> was launched in the European market in 2012, becoming the world's first <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">production</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel</a>-electric hybrid. According to <a href="/wiki/Peugeot" title="Peugeot">Peugeot</a> the new hybrid delivers a <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel economy</a> of up to 62&#160;miles per US gallon (3.8&#160;L/100&#160;km; 74&#160;mpg<sub><small>-imp</small></sub>) and CO<sub>2</sub> emissions of 99g/km on the European test cycle.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_v" title="Toyota Prius v">Toyota Prius v</a>, launched in the U.S. in October 2011, is the first spinoff from the <a href="/wiki/Prius" title="Prius" class="mw-redirect">Prius</a> family. Sales in Japan began in May 2011 as the Prius Alpha. The European version, named Prius +, was launched in June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The Prius Aqua was launched in Japan in December 2011, and was released as the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_c" title="Toyota Prius c">Toyota Prius c</a> in the U.S. in March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-LaunchUS_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaunchUS-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The Prius c was launched in Australia in April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The production version of the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Yaris Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Yaris Hybrid</a> went on sale in Europe in June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Other hybrids released in the U.S. during 2012 are the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Q5_Hybrid" title="Audi Q5 Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Audi Q5 Hybrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW_5_Series_ActiveHybrid" title="BMW 5 Series ActiveHybrid" class="mw-redirect">BMW 5 Series ActiveHybrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW_3_series_Hybrid" title="BMW 3 series Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">BMW 3 series Hybrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max_Hybrid" title="Ford C-Max Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford C-Max Hybrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acura_ILX" title="Acura ILX">Acura ILX Hybrid</a>. Also during 2012 were released the next generation of <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Camry_(XV50)#Camry_Hybrid" title="Toyota Camry (XV50)">Toyota Camry Hybrid</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid#Second_generation" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Ford Fusion Hybrid</a>, both of which offer significantly improved fuel economy in comparison with their previous generations.<sup id="cite_ref-USales0912_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USales0912-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GCC0812_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0812-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2013 models of the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Avalon_Hybrid" title="Toyota Avalon Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Avalon Hybrid</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Jetta_Hybrid" title="Volkswagen Jetta Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Volkswagen Jetta Hybrid</a> were released in the U.S. in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-USales2012_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USales2012-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Global sales of the Toyota Prius liftback passed the 3 million milestone in June 2013. The Prius liftbak is available in almost 80 countries and regions, and it is the world's best selling hybrid electric vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-Prius3mi_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prius3mi-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Toyota released the hybrid versions of the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Corolla_Axio" title="Toyota Corolla Axio" class="mw-redirect">Corolla Axio</a> sedan and <a href="/wiki/Corolla_Fielder" title="Corolla Fielder" class="mw-redirect">Corolla Fielder</a> station wagon in Japan in August 2013. Both cars are equipped with a 1.5-liter hybrid system similar to the one used in the Prius c.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_and_rankings">Sales and rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sales and rankings">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sales and rankings" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hibrid_Toyota_Prius_61_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Hibrid_Toyota_Prius_61_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg/220px-Hibrid_Toyota_Prius_61_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Hibrid_Toyota_Prius_61_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg/330px-Hibrid_Toyota_Prius_61_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Hibrid_Toyota_Prius_61_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg/440px-Hibrid_Toyota_Prius_61_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hibrid_Toyota_Prius_61_MIA_12_2008_with_logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> is the top selling hybrid in both the U.S. and Japan, with sales of more than 1 million units in each country.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of March 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, more than 6.3 million hybrid electric vehicles have been sold worldwide since their inception in 1997, led by <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Company" title="Toyota Motor Company" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Motor Company</a> (TMC) with 5.125 million <a href="/wiki/Lexus" title="Lexus">Lexus</a> and Toyota hybrids sold through March 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-TMC5miHEVs_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMC5miHEVs-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Honda_Motor_Co.,_Ltd." title="Honda Motor Co., Ltd." class="mw-redirect">Honda Motor Co., Ltd.</a> with cumulative global sales of more than 1 million hybrids by September 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Honda1mi_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honda1mi-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Corporation" title="Ford Motor Corporation" class="mw-redirect">Ford Motor Corporation</a> with more than 200 thousand hybrids sold in the United States by June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Ford200K_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ford200K-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> TMC experienced record sales of hybrid cars during 2012, with 1,028,900 million units sold from January 1 through October 31, 2012, representing 14% of TMC's global sales in the first ten months of the year. Also, cumulative year-to-date TMC's hybrid sales through October climbed 63.6% over 2011 total sales of 628,989 hybrids.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Toyota hybrids combined with Lexus models reached 1&#160;million hybrids sold in the U.S. by February 2009;<sup id="cite_ref-Toyota0109_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota0109-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> worldwide sales of hybrids by both brands totaled over 2&#160;million vehicles by August 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-Toyota0909_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota0909-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> 3&#160;million units by February 2011, and reached the 5&#160;million mark in March 2013. As of March 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, global hybrid sales are led by the <a href="/wiki/Prius_family" title="Prius family" class="mw-redirect">Prius family</a>, with sales of 3,671,800 units representing 71.6% of TMC worldwide sales, and the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> liftback, available in almost 80 countries, is the leading model with cumulative sales of over 3 million units through June 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Prius3mi_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prius3mi-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GCC102012_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC102012-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The hybrid model with the next highest cumulative sales is the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_c" title="Toyota Prius c">Toyota Prius c</a>/Aqua, with global sales of 409,500 units sold through March 2013., followed by the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Camry_Hybrid" title="Toyota Camry Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Camry Hybrid</a>, with 357,000 units sold through March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-TMC5miHEVs_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMC5miHEVs-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> U.S. sales of the Toyota Prius reached the 1.0 million milestone in early April 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-US1million_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US1million-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> and cumulative sales of the Prius in Japan exceeded the 1&#160;million mark in August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-JP1million_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP1million-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Global sales of Lexus brand hybrid vehicles worldwide reached the 500 thousand mark in November 2012, with the <a href="/wiki/Lexus_RX" title="Lexus RX">Lexus RX 400h/RX 450h</a> as the top selling Lexus hybrid with 259 thousand units, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Lexus_CT_200h" title="Lexus CT 200h" class="mw-redirect">Lexus CT 200h</a> with 122 thousand units.<sup id="cite_ref-Lexus500K_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lexus500K-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The United States is the leading hybrid market with about 2.7 million units sold through March 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-DoEHEV10_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DoEHEV10-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2011US_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011US-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> followed by Japan with more than 2 million units sold through October 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-TMCSales1012_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMCSales1012-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HondaHEV09_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HondaHEV09-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Insight100K_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Insight100K-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> with around 550 thousand hybrids by December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-HondaHEV09_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HondaHEV09-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ToyotaEU2012_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToyotaEU2012-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The top seller hybrid in the U.S. is the Toyota Prius, with cumulative sales of 1,267,166 units since 2000 through September 2012, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Civic_Hybrid" title="Honda Civic Hybrid">Honda Civic Hybrid</a>, with cumulative sales of 214,877 vehicles since 2002, and the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Camry_Hybrid" title="Toyota Camry Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Camry Hybrid</a>, with 213,096 units sold since 2006. The top selling hybrid in the U.S. by an American manufacturer is the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrid</a>, with cumulative sales of 130,691 vehicles since 2004, followed by the siblings <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKZ" title="Lincoln MKZ">Lincoln MKZ</a>/<a href="/wiki/Mercury_Milan" title="Mercury Milan">Mercury Milan</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Fusion Hybrids</a>, with combined sales of 70,536 units since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-DoEHEV10_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DoEHEV10-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2011US_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011US-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._market">U.S. market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: U.S. market">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: U.S. market" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicles_in_the_United_States" title="Hybrid electric vehicles in the United States">Hybrid electric vehicles in the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Escape_Hybrid_with_logo_5206_DC_03_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Ford_Escape_Hybrid_with_logo_5206_DC_03_2009.jpg/220px-Ford_Escape_Hybrid_with_logo_5206_DC_03_2009.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Ford_Escape_Hybrid_with_logo_5206_DC_03_2009.jpg/330px-Ford_Escape_Hybrid_with_logo_5206_DC_03_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Ford_Escape_Hybrid_with_logo_5206_DC_03_2009.jpg/440px-Ford_Escape_Hybrid_with_logo_5206_DC_03_2009.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Escape_Hybrid_with_logo_5206_DC_03_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrid</a> is the top selling hybrid in the U.S. from an American carmaker.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The fleet of <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicles_in_the_United_States" title="Hybrid electric vehicles in the United States">hybrid electric vehicles in the United States</a> is the largest in the world, and cumulative sales surpassed the 2 million mark in May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-US2mi_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2mi-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Since their inception in 1999, a total of 2,592,221 hybrid electric automobiles and SUVs have been sold through December 2012, led by the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> family with 1,315,469 units sold, representing a 50.7% <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of total hybrid sales.<sup id="cite_ref-DoEHEV10_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DoEHEV10-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2011US_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011US-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_99-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A total of 434,498 hybrid electric vehicles were sold during 2012, and the hybrid market share of total new car sales in the country was 3.0%, up from 2.1% in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_99-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The top selling hybrids, with more than 10,000 units sold during 2012, were the Toyota Prius liftback (147,503), the second generation <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Camry_(XV50)#Camry_Hybrid" title="Toyota Camry (XV50)">Toyota Camry Hybrid</a> (45,626), <a href="/wiki/Prius_v" title="Prius v" class="mw-redirect">Prius v</a> (40,669), <a href="/wiki/Prius_c" title="Prius c" class="mw-redirect">Prius c</a> (35,733), <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Sonata_Hybrid" title="Hyundai Sonata Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Hyundai Sonata Hybrid</a> (20,754), <a href="/wiki/Lexus_CT_200h" title="Lexus CT 200h" class="mw-redirect">Lexus CT 200h</a> (17,671), <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Malibu_Hybrid" title="Chevrolet Malibu Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Chevrolet Malibu Hybrid</a> (16,664), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Ford Fusion Hybrid</a> (14,100), <a href="/wiki/Lexus_RX" title="Lexus RX">Lexus RX400h/450h</a> (12,223), <a href="/wiki/Buick_LaCrosse#eAssist" title="Buick LaCrosse">Buick LaCrosse Hybrid</a> (12,010), <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max_Hybrid" title="Ford C-Max Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford C-Max Hybrid</a> (10,935), and the <a href="/wiki/Kia_Optima_Hybrid" title="Kia Optima Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Kia Optima Hybrid</a> (10,084).<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_99-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Toyota sold 223,905 Prii among the various HEV family members in the U.S. in 2012, representing together a market share of 51.5% of all hybrid sold in the country that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_99-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Out of the 5.125 million hybrids sold by <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Company" title="Toyota Motor Company" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Motor Company</a> worldwide through March 2013, the United States accounted for 1,951,243 units.<sup id="cite_ref-TMC5miHEVs_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMC5miHEVs-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> has been the state leading hybrid sales in the U.S. with 55,553 vehicles sold in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-dashboard09_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard09-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> 74,932 in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-dashboard08_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard08-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> and 91,417 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-dashboard07_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard07-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009 it was followed by <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a> (15,438) and <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> (14,949).<sup id="cite_ref-dashboard09_104-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard09-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of new hybrids sold <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a>, the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" title="District of Columbia" class="mw-redirect">District of Columbia</a> was the leader in 2009 with 3.79 hybrids per 1000 residents, followed by California (1.54) and <a href="/wiki/Washington_(U.S._state)" title="Washington (U.S. state)" class="mw-redirect">Washington</a> (1.53).<sup id="cite_ref-dashboard09_104-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard09-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The top 5 <a href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area" class="mw-redirect">U. S. metropolitan area</a> markets for sales of hybrid electric vehicles in 2009 were <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area" title="Greater Los Angeles Area">Los Angeles</a> (26,677), <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York</a> (21,193), <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco</a> (15,799), <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Washington Metropolitan Area" class="mw-redirect">Washington, D.C.</a> (11,595), and <a href="/wiki/Chicago_metropolitan_area" title="Chicago metropolitan area">Chicago</a> (8,990).<sup id="cite_ref-dashboard09_104-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard09-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> The following table summarizes the top metropolitan area markets in terms of new hybrids sold per capita.</p>
