<p>Considering hybrid sales between January 2010 through September 2011, the top selling metropolitan region was the San Francisco Bay Area, with 8.4% of all new cars sold during that period, followed by <a href="/wiki/Monterey_County" title="Monterey County" class="mw-redirect">Monterey-Salinas</a> with 6.9%, and <a href="/wiki/Eugene,_Oregon" title="Eugene, Oregon">Eugene, Oregon</a>, with 6.1%. The following seven top selling markets are also on the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Seattle_metropolitan_area" title="Seattle metropolitan area">Seattle-Tacoma</a> and Los Angeles with 5.7%, San Diego with 5.6%, and Portland with 5.4%. The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Washington Metropolitan Area" class="mw-redirect">Washington D.C. Metro Area</a>, with 4.2%, is the next best selling region out of the West Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sales of <a href="/wiki/Prius_family" title="Prius family" class="mw-redirect">Prius family</a> vehicles in California represented 25% of all Prii purchases in the U.S. during the first nine months of 2012. With 46,380 units sold during this period, the Prius family became the best selling <a href="/wiki/Nameplate" title="Nameplate">nameplate</a> in California, ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Civic" title="Honda Civic">Honda Civic</a> (43,143 units) and the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Accord" title="Honda Accord">Honda Accord</a> (39,027 units).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of November 2012, Toyota USA estimates that sales of its hybrids models in 2012 will represent 14% of total Toyota sales in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japanese_market">Japanese market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Japanese market">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Japanese market" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>'s hybrid sales in Japan since 1997, including both Toyota and Lexus models, passed the 1 million mark in July 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-Toyota0710_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota0710-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> and reached 2 million in October 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-TMCSales1012_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMCSales1012-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Cumulative sales of the original Prius in Japan reached the 1&#160;million mark in August 2011<sup id="cite_ref-JP1million_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP1million-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> and sales of the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius#Prius_family" title="Toyota Prius">Prius family</a> vehicles reached 1,639,800 units in October 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-TMCSales1012_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMCSales1012-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Cumulative sales of <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a>'s hybrid vehicles since November 1999 reached 25,239 units by January 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-HondaHEV09_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HondaHEV09-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> and in March 2010, Honda announced that the new 2010 <a href="/wiki/Honda_Insight" title="Honda Insight">Insight</a> broke through 100,000 sales in Japan in just one year after its introduction.<sup id="cite_ref-Insight100K_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Insight100K-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TOYOTA_PRIUS%CE%B1_ZVW41_REAR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/TOYOTA_PRIUS%CE%B1_ZVW41_REAR.jpg/220px-TOYOTA_PRIUS%CE%B1_ZVW41_REAR.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/TOYOTA_PRIUS%CE%B1_ZVW41_REAR.jpg/330px-TOYOTA_PRIUS%CE%B1_ZVW41_REAR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/TOYOTA_PRIUS%CE%B1_ZVW41_REAR.jpg/440px-TOYOTA_PRIUS%CE%B1_ZVW41_REAR.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TOYOTA_PRIUS%CE%B1_ZVW41_REAR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_%CE%B1" title="Toyota Prius α" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Prius α</a> was launched in Japan in May 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hybrid sales in Japan almost tripled in 2009 as compared to 2008 as a result of government incentives that included a <a href="/wiki/Scrappage_program#Japan" title="Scrappage program">scrappage program</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle#Japan" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">tax breaks</a> on hybrid vehicles and other low emission cars and trucks, and a higher levy on gasoline that rose prices in the order of US$4.50.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Polk2009_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Polk2009-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Japan_US_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_US-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> New hybrid car sales jumped from 94,259 in 2008<sup id="cite_ref-dashboard08_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashboard08-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> to 334,000 in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-Tot2009_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tot2009-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> and hybrid sales in 2009 represented around 10% of new vehicles sales in Japan. In contrast, the U.S. market share was 2.8% for the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> These record sales allowed Japan to surpass the U.S. in total new hybrid sales, with the Japanese market representing almost half (48%) of the worldwide hybrid sales in 2009 while the U.S. market represented 42% of global sales.<sup id="cite_ref-Tot2009_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tot2009-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> became the first hybrid to top annual new car sales in Japan with 208,876 units sold in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTPrius10_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTPrius10-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> The Insight ranked fifth in overall sales in 2009 with 93,283 units sold.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A total of 315,669 Prii were sold domestically in 2010, making the Prius the country's best-selling vehicle for the second straight year. Also the Prius broke Japan's annual sales record for a single model for the first time in 20 years, surpassing the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Corolla" title="Toyota Corolla">Toyota Corolla</a>, which in 1990 set the previous sales record with 300,008 units.<sup id="cite_ref-Jap2010_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jap2010-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> The Prius sold 252,528 units in 2011, becoming the best-selling vehicle for the third-consecutive year. This figure includes sales of the <a href="/wiki/Prius_%CE%B1" title="Prius α" class="mw-redirect">Prius α</a>, launched in May 2011, and the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Aqua" title="Toyota Aqua" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Aqua</a>, launched in December. Despite keeping to the top selling spot, total Prius sales for 2011 were 20% lower than 2010 due partly to the disruptions caused by the March <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami</a>, and also because government incentives for hybrid cars were scaled back.<sup id="cite_ref-Jap2011_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jap2011-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, during the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year#Japan" title="Fiscal year">Japanese fiscal year</a> (April 1, 2011 through March 31, 2012), hybrid vehicles accounted for 16% of all new car sales in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 2012, hybrid sales reached a record market share of 19.7% of new car sales in the country, including <a href="/wiki/Kei_car" title="Kei car">kei cars</a>. Sales were led by the conventional Prius followed by the Toyota Aqua. Also during this month, hybrid sales represented 25% of Honda sales and 46% of Toyota sales in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_market">European market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: European market">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: European market" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sales of hybrids in Europe went up from around 9,000 units in 2004 to 39,880 in 2006, with Toyota accounting for 91% of hybrid sales and Honda with 3,410 units sold that year. Cumulative sales of Toyota hybrids since 2000 reached 69,674 units in 2006, while Honda hybrid sales reached over 8,000 units.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> By January 2009, Honda had sold 35,149 hybrids in Europe, of which 34,757 were <a href="/wiki/Honda_Civic_Hybrid" title="Honda Civic Hybrid">Honda Civic Hybrids</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HondaHEV09_101-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HondaHEV09-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> During 2008 combined sales of Toyota and Lexus hybrids in Europe were 57,819 units, representing 5.2% of total Toyota sales in the region. Toyota sales were led by Prius with 41,495 units.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Cumulative sales of the Toyota Prius reached 100,000 units in 2008 and the 200,000 mark was reached in July 2010. The UK has been one of the leading European markets for the Prius since its inception, with 20% of Prius sales in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Toyota's European hybrid sales reached 70,529 vehicles in 2010, including sales of 15,237 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Auris_Hybrid" title="Toyota Auris Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Auris Hybrids</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Sales reached 84,839 units in 2011, including 59,161 Toyota and 25,678 Lexus hybrid vehicles. The Auris hybrid sold 32,725 units in 2011. Lexus hybrids made up 85% of total sales in Western Europe in 2011. Toyota and Lexus hybrids represented 10% percent of Toyota's European new car sales in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Toyota35mi_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota35mi-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> As of December 2012, Toyota Motor Company has sold more than 500,000 Lexus and Toyota hybrids in Europe since the introduction of the Prius in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-ToyotaEU2012_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToyotaEU2012-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of December 2011, the total number of hybrids registered in the UK since 2006 reached 100,455 vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-UK201011_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK201011-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UK200906_116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK200906-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Honda has sold in the UK more than 22,000 hybrid cars since the Insight was launched in the country in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> On 1 January 2010, there were 39.3 thousand hybrid cars registered in the Netherlands, up from 23 thousand the previous year. Most of the registered hybrid cars belong to corporate fleets due to tax incentives established in the country in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-NED2009_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NED2009-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> A total of 48,587 hybrid cars have been registered in France since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FRA2011_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2011-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FRA2010_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2010-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FRA200908_112-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRA200908-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FRA2007_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2007-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the 13,340 units registered in 2011, the top selling models in the French market were the Toyota Auris (4,740 units), the Prius (2,429 units), and the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Jazz_Hybrid" title="Honda Jazz Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Honda Jazz Hybrid</a> (1,857 units). The <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_3008_HYbrid4" title="Peugeot 3008 HYbrid4" class="mw-redirect">Peugeot 3008 HYbrid4</a>, launched in late 2011, sold 401 units.<sup id="cite_ref-FRA2011_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRA2011-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> The total number of registered hybrid cars in Germany reached 47,642 vehicles on January 1, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> A total of 10,350 hybrid cars were registered in Spain in 2011, up 22% from 2010 sales. The top selling hybrids were the Toyota Prius, Toyota Auris HSD and the <a href="/wiki/Lexus_CT_200h" title="Lexus CT 200h" class="mw-redirect">Lexus CT 200h</a>, which together represented 83,2% of new hybrid car sales in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Technology">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Technology" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The varieties of hybrid electric designs can be differentiated by the structure of the <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle_drivetrain" title="Hybrid vehicle drivetrain">hybrid vehicle drivetrain</a>, the fuel type, and the mode of operation.</p>
<p>In 2007, several automobile manufacturers announced that future vehicles will use aspects of hybrid electric technology to reduce fuel consumption without the use of the hybrid drivetrain. Regenerative braking can be used to recapture energy and stored to power electrical accessories, such as air conditioning. Shutting down the engine at idle can also be used to reduce fuel consumption and reduce emissions without the addition of a hybrid drivetrain. In both cases, some of the advantages of hybrid electric technology are gained while additional cost and weight may be limited to the addition of larger batteries and starter motors. There is no standard terminology for such vehicles, although they may be termed <a href="/wiki/Mild_hybrid" title="Mild hybrid">mild hybrids</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Engines_and_fuel_sources">Engines and fuel sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Engines and fuel sources">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Engines and fuel sources" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fossil_fuels">Fossil fuels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fossil fuels">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fossil fuels" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">Fossil fuel</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Free-piston_engine" title="Free-piston engine">Free-piston engines</a> could be used to generate electricity as efficiently as, and less expensively than, fuel cells.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Gasoline</dt>
</dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gasoline_engine" title="Gasoline engine" class="mw-redirect">Gasoline engines</a> are used in most hybrid electric designs and will likely remain dominant for the foreseeable future.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> While <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>-derived gasoline is the primary fuel, it is possible to mix in varying levels of ethanol created from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> sources. Like most modern <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICE</a> powered vehicles, HEVs can typically use up to about 15% <a href="/wiki/Bioethanol" title="Bioethanol" class="mw-redirect">bioethanol</a>. Manufacturers may move to <a href="/wiki/Flexible_fuel_engine" title="Flexible fuel engine" class="mw-redirect">flexible fuel engines</a>, which would increase allowable ratios, but no plans are in place at present.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Diesel</dt>
</dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric" title="Diesel-electric" class="mw-redirect">Diesel-electric</a> HEVs use a <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engine</a> for power generation. Diesels have advantages when delivering constant power for long periods of time, suffering less wear while operating at higher efficiency. The diesel engine's high torque, combined with hybrid technology, may offer substantially improved mileage. Most diesel vehicles can use 100% pure <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuels</a> (<a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a>), so they can use but do not need <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> at all for fuel (although mixes of biofuel and petroleum are more common). If diesel-electric HEVs were in use, this benefit would likely also apply. Diesel-electric hybrid drivetrains have begun to appear in commercial vehicles (particularly buses); as of 2007, no light duty diesel-electric hybrid passenger cars are currently available, although prototypes exist. Peugeot is expected to produce a diesel-electric hybrid version of its 308 in late 2008 for the European market.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citro%C3%ABn" title="PSA Peugeot Citroën">PSA Peugeot Citroën</a> has unveiled two demonstrator vehicles featuring a diesel-electric hybrid drivetrain: the <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_307" title="Peugeot 307">Peugeot 307</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_C4" title="Citroën C4">Citroën C4</a> Hybride HDi and <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_C-Cactus" title="Citroën C-Cactus">Citroën C-Cactus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> made a <a href="/wiki/Prototype" title="Prototype">prototype</a> diesel-electric hybrid car that achieved 2&#160;L/100&#160;km (140&#160;mpg<sub><small>-imp</small></sub>; 120&#160;mpg<sub><small>-US</small></sub>) fuel economy, but has yet to sell a hybrid vehicle. <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Corporation" title="General Motors Corporation" class="mw-redirect">General Motors</a> has been testing the <a href="/wiki/Opel_Astra" title="Opel Astra">Opel Astra</a> Diesel Hybrid. There have been no concrete dates suggested for these vehicles, but press statements have suggested production vehicles would not appear before 2009.</p>
<p>At the Frankfurt Motor Show in September 2009 both Mercedes and BMW displayed diesel-electric hybrids.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Robert Bosch GmbH</a> is supplying hybrid diesel-electric technology to diverse automakers and models, including the <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_308" title="Peugeot 308">Peugeot 308</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>So far, production diesel-electric engines have mostly<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="You can help — (March 2009)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup> appeared in <a href="/wiki/Mass_transit" title="Mass transit" class="mw-redirect">mass transit</a> buses.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/FedEx" title="FedEx">FedEx</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Eaton_Corporation" title="Eaton Corporation">Eaton Corp.</a> in the USA and <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco</a> in Europe, has begun deploying a small fleet of Hybrid diesel electric delivery trucks.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> As of October 2007, Fedex operates more than 100 diesel electric hybrids in North America, Asia and Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Liquefied petroleum gas</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20100728_hyundai_avante_lpi_hybrid_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/20100728_hyundai_avante_lpi_hybrid_02.jpg/220px-20100728_hyundai_avante_lpi_hybrid_02.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/20100728_hyundai_avante_lpi_hybrid_02.jpg/330px-20100728_hyundai_avante_lpi_hybrid_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/20100728_hyundai_avante_lpi_hybrid_02.jpg/440px-20100728_hyundai_avante_lpi_hybrid_02.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20100728_hyundai_avante_lpi_hybrid_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Elantra_LPI_Hybrid" title="Hyundai Elantra LPI Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Hyundai Elantra LPI Hybrid</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hyundai" title="Hyundai">Hyundai</a> introduced in 2009 the <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Elantra_LPI_Hybrid" title="Hyundai Elantra LPI Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Hyundai Elantra LPI Hybrid</a>, which is the first <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">mass production</a> hybrid electric vehicle to run on <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas" title="Liquefied petroleum gas">liquefied petroleum gas</a> (LPG).<sup id="cite_ref-Hyundai0709_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hyundai0709-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Hydrogen</dt>
</dl>
<p>Hydrogen can be used in cars in two ways: a source of combustible heat, or a source of electrons for an electric motor. The burning of hydrogen is not being developed in practical terms; it is the hydrogen fuel-cell electric vehicle (HFEV) which is garnering all the attention. <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_fuel_cells" title="Hydrogen fuel cells" class="mw-redirect">Hydrogen fuel cells</a> create electricity fed into an electric motor to drives the wheels. Hydrogen is not burned, but it is consumed. This means molecular hydrogen, H<sub>2</sub>, is combined with oxygen to form water. 2H<sub>2</sub> (4e<sup>-</sup>) + O<sub>2</sub> --&gt; 2H<sub>2</sub>O (4e<sup>-</sup>). The molecular hydrogen and oxygen's mutual affinity drives the fuel cell to separate the electrons from the hydrogen, to use them to power the electric motor, and to return them to the ionized water molecules that were formed when the electron-depleted hydrogen combined with the oxygen in the fuel cell. Recalling that a hydrogen atom is nothing more than a proton and an electron; in essence, the motor is driven by the proton's atomic attraction to the oxygen nucleus, and the electron's attraction to the ionized water molecule.</p>
<p>An HFEV is an all-electric car featuring an open-source battery in the form of a hydrogen tank and the atmosphere. HFEVs may also comprise closed-cell batteries for the purpose of power storage from regenerative braking, but this does not change the source of the motivation. It implies the HFEV is an electric car with two types of batteries. Since HFEVs are purely electric, and do not contain any type of heat engine, they are not hybrids.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Biofuels">Biofuels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Biofuels">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Biofuels" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flexifuel_vehicle" title="Flexifuel vehicle" class="mw-redirect">flexifuel vehicle</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Escape_E85_Flex_Fuel_Hybrid_WAS_2010_8941.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Escape_E85_Flex_Fuel_Hybrid_WAS_2010_8941.JPG/220px-Escape_E85_Flex_Fuel_Hybrid_WAS_2010_8941.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Escape_E85_Flex_Fuel_Hybrid_WAS_2010_8941.JPG/330px-Escape_E85_Flex_Fuel_Hybrid_WAS_2010_8941.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Escape_E85_Flex_Fuel_Hybrid_WAS_2010_8941.JPG/440px-Escape_E85_Flex_Fuel_Hybrid_WAS_2010_8941.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Escape_E85_Flex_Fuel_Hybrid_WAS_2010_8941.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrid</a> was the first hybrid electric vehicle with a <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible-fuel vehicle">flex-fuel engine</a> capable of running on <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> fuel.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Escape_E85_Flex_Plug-in_Hybrid_views_and_badging_WAS_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ford_Escape_E85_Flex_Plug-in_Hybrid_views_and_badging_WAS_2010.jpg/220px-Ford_Escape_E85_Flex_Plug-in_Hybrid_views_and_badging_WAS_2010.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ford_Escape_E85_Flex_Plug-in_Hybrid_views_and_badging_WAS_2010.jpg/330px-Ford_Escape_E85_Flex_Plug-in_Hybrid_views_and_badging_WAS_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ford_Escape_E85_Flex_Plug-in_Hybrid_views_and_badging_WAS_2010.jpg/440px-Ford_Escape_E85_Flex_Plug-in_Hybrid_views_and_badging_WAS_2010.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Escape_E85_Flex_Plug-in_Hybrid_views_and_badging_WAS_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Demonstration <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape</a> <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> flex-fuel <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hybrid vehicles might use an <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> running on <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuels</a>, such as a <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel" title="Flexible-fuel" class="mw-redirect">flexible-fuel</a> engine running on <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a> or engines running on <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a>. In 2007 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Corporation" title="Ford Motor Corporation" class="mw-redirect">Ford</a> produced 20 demonstration <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Escape Hybrid</a> E85s for real-world testing in fleets in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> Also as a demonstration project, Ford delivered in 2008 the first flexible-fuel <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> <a href="/wiki/SUV" title="SUV" class="mw-redirect">SUV</a> to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Energy" title="U.S. Department of Energy" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Department of Energy</a> (DOE), a <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Plug-in Hybrid</a>, capable of running on gasoline or E85.<sup id="cite_ref-FlesFuelHybrid_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FlesFuelHybrid-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a> <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in hybrid electric vehicle" class="mw-redirect">plug-in hybrid electric vehicle</a> would be the first commercially available flex-fuel plug-in hybrid capable of adapting the propulsion to the biofuels used in several world markets such as the ethanol blend <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> in the U.S., or <a href="/wiki/Neat_alcohol_fuel" title="Neat alcohol fuel" class="mw-redirect">E100</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, or biodiesel in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GMVoltFlex_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMVoltFlex-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Green0107_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Green0107-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> The Volt will be <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> <a href="/wiki/Flex-fuel" title="Flex-fuel" class="mw-redirect">flex-fuel</a> capable about a year after its introduction.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_machines">Electric machines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Electric machines">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Electric machines" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <i>split path</i> vehicles (Toyota, Ford, GM, Chrysler) there are two electrical machines, one of which functions as a motor primarily, and the other functions as a generator primarily. One of the primary requirements of these machines is that they are very efficient, as the electrical portion of the energy must be converted from the engine to the generator, through two <a href="/wiki/Power_inverter" title="Power inverter">inverters</a>, through the motor again and then to the wheels.</p>
<p>Most of the electric machines used in hybrid vehicles are <a href="/wiki/Brushless_DC_motor" title="Brushless DC motor" class="mw-redirect">brushless DC motors</a> (BLDC). Specifically, they are of a type called an interior permanent magnet (IPM) machine (or motor). These machines are wound similarly to the induction motors found in a typical home, but (for high efficiency) use very strong rare earth magnets in the rotor. These magnets contain <a href="/wiki/Neodymium" title="Neodymium">neodymium</a>, iron and boron, and are therefore called <a href="/wiki/Neodymium_magnet" title="Neodymium magnet">Neodymium magnets</a>. The magnet material is expensive, and its cost is one of the limiting factors in the use of these machines.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Design_considerations">Design considerations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Design considerations">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Design considerations" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In some cases, manufacturers are producing HEVs that use the added energy provided by the hybrid systems to give vehicles a power boost, rather than significantly improved fuel efficiency compared to their traditional counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> The trade-off between added performance and improved fuel efficiency is partly controlled by the software within the hybrid system and partly the result of the engine, battery and motor size. In the future, manufacturers may provide HEV owners with the ability to partially control this balance (fuel efficiency vs. added performance) as they wish, through a user-controlled setting.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> Toyota announced in January, 2006 that it was considering a "high-efficiency" button.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conversion_kits">Conversion kits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Conversion kits">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Conversion kits" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_conversion" title="Electric vehicle conversion">Electric vehicle conversion</a></div>
<p>One can buy a stock hybrid or convert a stock petroleum car to a hybrid electric vehicle using an <a href="/wiki/Aftermarket_kit" title="Aftermarket kit" class="mw-redirect">aftermarket hybrid kit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_impact">Environmental impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Environmental impact">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Environmental impact" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_consumption">Fuel consumption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fuel consumption">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fuel consumption" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">Fuel efficiency</a></div>
<p>Current HEVs reduce petroleum consumption under certain circumstances, compared to otherwise similar conventional vehicles, primarily by using three mechanisms:<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li>Reducing wasted energy during idle/low output, generally by turning the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICE</a> off</li>
<li>Recapturing waste energy (i.e. regenerative braking)</li>
<li>Reducing the size and power of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICE</a>, and hence inefficiencies from under-utilization, by using the added power from the electric motor to compensate for the loss in peak power output from the smaller <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICE</a>.</li>
</ol>
<p>Any combination of these three primary hybrid advantages may be used in different vehicles to realize different fuel usage, power, emissions, weight and cost profiles. The <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICE</a> in an HEV can be smaller, lighter, and more efficient than the one in a conventional vehicle, because the combustion engine can be sized for slightly above <i>average</i> power demand rather than <i>peak</i> power demand. The drive system in a vehicle is required to operate over a range of speed and power, but an <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICE</a>'s highest efficiency is in a narrow range of operation, making conventional vehicles inefficient. On the contrary, in most HEV designs, the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICE</a> operates closer to its range of highest efficiency more frequently. The power curve of electric motors is better suited to variable speeds and can provide substantially greater torque at low speeds compared with internal-combustion engines. The greater <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel economy</a> of HEVs has implication for reduced petroleum consumption and <a href="/wiki/Roadway_air_dispersion_modeling" title="Roadway air dispersion modeling">vehicle air pollution emissions</a> worldwide<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noise">Noise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Noise">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Noise" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_warning_sounds" title="Electric vehicle warning sounds">Electric vehicle warning sounds</a></div>
<p>Reduced noise emissions resulting from substantial use of the electric motor at idling and low speeds, leading to <a href="/wiki/Roadway_noise" title="Roadway noise">roadway</a> <a href="/wiki/Noise_mitigation" title="Noise mitigation" class="mw-redirect">noise reduction</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> in comparison to conventional gasoline or diesel powered engine vehicles, resulting in beneficial <a href="/wiki/Noise_health_effects" title="Noise health effects" class="mw-redirect">noise health effects</a> (although road noise from tires and wind, the loudest noises at highway speeds from the interior of most vehicles, are not affected by the hybrid design alone).</p>
<p>Reduced noise may not be beneficial for all road users, as blind people or the visually impaired consider the noise of combustion engines a helpful aid while crossing streets and feel quiet hybrids could pose an unexpected hazard.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Congress</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> are exploring legislation to establish a minimum level of sound for <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric</a> and hybrid electric vehicles when operating in electric mode, so that blind people and other pedestrians and cyclists can hear them coming and detect from which direction they are approaching. Tests have shown that vehicles operating in electric mode can be particularly hard to hear below 20&#160;mph (32&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2010 the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Land,_Infrastructure,_Transport_and_Tourism_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism (Japan)" class="mw-redirect">Japanese Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism</a> issued guidelines for hybrid and other near-silent vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-TMC0810_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMC0810-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A 2009 study conducted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">U.S. National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> found that crashes involving pedestrian and bicyclist have higher incidence rates for hybrids than <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> vehicles in certain vehicle maneuvers. These accidents commonly occurred on in zones with low speed limits, during daytime and in clear weather.<sup id="cite_ref-NHTSA_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHTSA-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Even though no specific national regulation has been enacted in most countries as of mid-2010, some carmakers announced they have decided to address this safety issue shared by regular hybrids and all types of <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric vehicles</a>, and as a result, the upcoming <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf#Warning_sounds" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a>, both due in late 2010, and the new <a href="/wiki/Infiniti_M#Hybrid_version_.282011.E2.80.93.29" title="Infiniti M">Nissan Fuga hybrid</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fisker_Karma" title="Fisker Karma">Fisker Karma</a> <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a>, both due in 2011, will include synthesized sounds to alert pedestrians, the blind and others to their presence.<sup id="cite_ref-NissanNoise_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NissanNoise-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutoBlogNoise_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBlogNoise-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT101309_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT101309-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There is also <a href="/wiki/After-market_(general)" title="After-market (general)" class="mw-redirect">aftermarket</a> technology available in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> to make hybrids sound more like conventional <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">combustion engine</a> cars when the vehicle goes into the silent <a href="/wiki/All-electric_mode" title="All-electric mode" class="mw-redirect">electric mode</a> (EV mode).<sup id="cite_ref-SciAm0808_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SciAm0808-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 2010 Toyota began sales in Japan of an onboard device designed to automatically emit a synthesized sound of an electric motor when the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Prius</a> is operating as an <a href="/wiki/All-electric_mode" title="All-electric mode" class="mw-redirect">electric vehicle</a> at speeds up to approximately 25 kilometres per hour (16&#160;mph). Toyota plans to use other versions of the device for use in gasoline-electric hybrids, plug-in hybrids, <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Fuel-cell" title="Fuel-cell" class="mw-redirect">fuel-cell</a> hybrid vehicles planned for <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">mass production</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TMC0810_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMC0810-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution">Pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Pollution">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Pollution" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_Scorecard" title="Hybrid Scorecard">Hybrid Scorecard</a></div>
<table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" style="" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width: 52px;"><img alt="Globe icon." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" width="48" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text" style=""><span class="mbox-text-span">The examples and perspective in this article <b>deal primarily with the United States and do not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> and discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Talk:Hybrid electric vehicle">talk page</a>.</span> <small><i>(December 2010)</i></small> </span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Battery toxicity is a concern, although today's hybrids use <a href="/wiki/NiMH" title="NiMH" class="mw-redirect">NiMH</a> batteries, not the environmentally problematic rechargeable <a href="/wiki/NiCd" title="NiCd" class="mw-redirect">nickel cadmium</a>. "Nickel metal hydride batteries are benign. They can be fully recycled," says Ron Cogan, editor of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Car_Journal" title="Green Car Journal">Green Car Journal</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Quotations" title="Wikipedia:Quotations"><span title="The text near this tag needs citation. (May 2008)">this quote needs a citation</span></a></i>]</sup> Toyota and Honda say that they will recycle dead batteries and that disposal will pose no toxic hazards. Toyota puts a phone number on each battery, and they pay a $200 "bounty" for each battery to help ensure that it will be properly recycled.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vehicle_types">Vehicle types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Vehicle types">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Vehicle types" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorcycles">Motorcycles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Motorcycles">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Motorcycles" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Companies such as <a href="/wiki/Zero_Motorcycles" title="Zero Motorcycles">Zero Motorcycles</a><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vectrix" title="Vectrix">Vectrix</a> have market-ready <a href="/wiki/All-electric_motorcycle" title="All-electric motorcycle" class="mw-redirect">all-electric motorcycles</a> available now, but the pairing of electrical components and an <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> (ICE) has made packaging <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cumbersome" class="extiw" title="wikt:cumbersome">cumbersome</a>, especially for niche brands.<sup id="cite_ref-sema.org_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sema.org-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Also, eCycle Inc produces series <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric" title="Diesel-electric" class="mw-redirect">diesel-electric</a> motorcycles, with a top speed of 80&#160;mph (130&#160;km/h) and a target retail price of $5500.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Peugeot_HYmotion3_compressor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peugeot HYmotion3 compressor (page does not exist)">Peugeot HYmotion3 compressor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> a hybrid <a href="/wiki/Scooter_(motorcycle)" title="Scooter (motorcycle)">scooter</a> is a three-wheeler that uses two separate power sources to power the front and back wheels. The back wheel is powered by a single cylinder 125 cc, 20&#160;bhp (15&#160;kW) single cylinder motor while the front wheels are each driven by their own <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a>. When the bike is moving up to 10&#160;km/h only the electric motors are used on a <a href="/wiki/Stop-start" title="Stop-start" class="mw-redirect">stop-start</a> basis reducing the amount of carbon emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/SEMA" title="SEMA">SEMA</a> has announced that <a href="/wiki/Yamaha" title="Yamaha" class="mw-redirect">Yamaha</a> is going to launch one in 2010, with <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> following a year later, fueling a competition to reign in new customers and set new standards for mobility. Each company hopes to provide the capability to reach 60 miles (97&#160;km) per charge by adopting advanced <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion" title="Lithium-ion" class="mw-redirect">lithium-ion</a> batteries to accomplish their claims. These proposed hybrid motorcycles could incorporate components from the upcoming <a href="/wiki/Honda_Insight" title="Honda Insight">Honda Insight</a> car and its hybrid powertrain. The ability to mass-produce these items helps to overcome the investment hurdles faced by <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">start-up</a> brands and bring new engineering concepts into <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_market" title="Mainstream market" class="mw-redirect">mainstream markets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sema.org_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sema.org-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automobiles_and_light_trucks">Automobiles and light trucks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Automobiles and light trucks">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Automobiles and light trucks" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hybrid_vehicles" title="List of hybrid vehicles">List of hybrid vehicles</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_performance_cars">High performance cars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: High performance cars">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: High performance cars" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As emissions regulations become tougher for manufacturers to adhere to, a new generation of high-performance cars will be powered by hybrid technology (for example the Porsche GT3 hybrid racing car). Aside from the emissions benefits of a hybrid system, the immediately available torque which is produced from electric motor(s) can lead to performance benefits by addressing the power curve weaknesses of a traditional combustion engine.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxis">Taxis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Taxis">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Taxis" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_taxi" title="Hybrid taxi">Hybrid taxi</a></div>
