</div>
</div>
<p>In 2000 <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>'s first hybrid electric taxi was put into service in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, operating a 2001 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> which traveled over 332,000 kilometres (206,000&#160;mi) before being retired.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of the major cities in the world are adding hybrid taxis to their taxicab fleets, led by <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenCG1_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenCG1-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> By 2009 15% of New York's 13,237 taxis in service are hybrids, the most in any city in North America, and also began retiring its original hybrid fleet after 300,000 and 350,000 miles (480,000 and 560,000 km) per vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenCG1_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenCG1-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> Other cities where taxi service is available with hybrid vehicles include <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Buses">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Buses" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_bus" title="Hybrid electric bus">Hybrid electric bus</a></div>
<p>Hybrid technology for buses has seen increased attention since recent battery developments decreased battery weight significantly. Drivetrains consist of conventional diesel engines and gas turbines. Some designs concentrate on using car engines, recent designs have focused on using conventional diesel engines already used in bus designs, to save on engineering and training costs. Several manufacturers are currently working on new hybrid designs, or hybrid drivetrains that fit into existing chassis offerings without major re-design. A challenge to hybrid buses may still come from cheaper lightweight imports from the former Eastern block countries or China, where national operators are looking at fuel consumption issues surrounding the weight of the bus, which has increased with recent bus technology innovations such as glazing, air conditioning and electrical systems. A hybrid bus can also deliver fuel economy though through the hybrid drivetrain. Hybrid technology is also being promoted by environmentally concerned transit authorities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trucks">Trucks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Trucks">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Trucks" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_truck" title="Hybrid electric truck">Hybrid electric truck</a></div>
<p>In 2003, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">GM</a> introduced a hybrid <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric" title="Diesel-electric" class="mw-redirect">diesel-electric</a> military (light) truck, equipped with a diesel electric and a fuel cell auxiliary power unit. Hybrid electric light trucks were introduced in 2004 by <a href="/wiki/Mercedes_Benz" title="Mercedes Benz" class="mw-redirect">Mercedes Benz</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Sprinter" title="Mercedes-Benz Sprinter">Sprinter</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Micro-Vett_SPA" title="Micro-Vett SPA" class="mw-redirect">Micro-Vett SPA</a> (Daily Bimodale). <a href="/wiki/Navistar_International" title="Navistar International">International Truck and Engine Corp.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eaton_Corp." title="Eaton Corp." class="mw-redirect">Eaton Corp.</a> have been selected to manufacture diesel-electric hybrid trucks for a US pilot program serving the utility industry in 2004. In mid-2005 <a href="/wiki/Isuzu" title="Isuzu" class="mw-redirect">Isuzu</a> introduced the Elf Diesel Hybrid Truck on the Japanese Market. They claim that approximately 300 vehicles, mostly route buses are using Hinos HIMR (Hybrid Inverter Controlled Motor &amp; Retarder) system. In 2007, high petroleum price means a hard sell for hybrid trucks<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> and appears the first U.S. production hybrid truck (International DuraStar Hybrid).<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:165Hybrid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/165Hybrid.jpg/220px-165Hybrid.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/165Hybrid.jpg/330px-165Hybrid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/165Hybrid.jpg/440px-165Hybrid.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:165Hybrid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hino_Motors" title="Hino Motors">Hino</a> hybrid <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric" title="Diesel-electric" class="mw-redirect">diesel-electric</a> truck.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other vehicles are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Big mining machines like the <a href="/wiki/Liebherr_T_282B" title="Liebherr T 282B">Liebherr T 282B</a> dump truck or Keaton Vandersteen <a href="/wiki/LeTourneau_L-2350" title="LeTourneau L-2350">LeTourneau L-2350</a> <a href="/wiki/Wheel_loader" title="Wheel loader" class="mw-redirect">wheel loader</a> are powered that way. Also there was several models of <a href="/wiki/BelAZ" title="BelAZ">BelAZ</a> (7530 and 7560 series) in <a href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR" class="mw-redirect">USSR</a> (now in <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>) since the middle of 1970th.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s huge <a href="/wiki/Crawler-Transporter" title="Crawler-Transporter" class="mw-redirect">Crawler-Transporters</a> are diesel-electric.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Fuso_Canter_Eco_Hybrid" title="Mitsubishi Fuso Canter Eco Hybrid">Mitsubishi Fuso Canter Eco Hybrid</a> is a diesel-electric commercial truck.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azure_Dynamics" title="Azure Dynamics">Azure Dynamics</a> Balance Hybrid Electric is a gasonline-hybrid electric medium dutry truck based on the Ford E-450 chassis.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hino_Motors" title="Hino Motors">Hino Motors</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> subsidiary) has the world's first production hybrid electric truck in Australia (110 kW or 150&#160;hp diesel engine plus a 23 kW or 31&#160;hp <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Other hybrid petroleum-electric truck makers are <a href="/wiki/DAF_Trucks" title="DAF Trucks">DAF Trucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN AG</a> with <a href="/w/index.php?title=MAN_TGL_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MAN TGL Series (page does not exist)">MAN TGL Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Motors" title="Nissan Motors" class="mw-redirect">Nissan Motors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Renault_Trucks" title="Renault Trucks">Renault Trucks</a> with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Renault_Puncher&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Renault Puncher (page does not exist)">Renault Puncher</a>.</p>
<p>Hybrid electric truck technology and <a href="/wiki/Powertrain" title="Powertrain">powertrain</a> maker: <a href="/wiki/ZF_Friedrichshafen" title="ZF Friedrichshafen">ZF Friedrichshafen</a>.</p>
<p>By a <a href="/wiki/Voice_vote" title="Voice vote">voice vote</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a> approved the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hdl.loc.gov/loc.uscongress/legislation.111hr445">Heavy Duty Hybrid Vehicle Research, Development, and Demonstration Act of 2009</a> ( for <a href="/wiki/Truck_classification" title="Truck classification">heavy duty</a> <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_vehicle" title="Plug-in hybrid vehicle" class="mw-redirect">plug-in hybrid vehicles</a>) authored by representative <a href="/wiki/James_Sensenbrenner" title="James Sensenbrenner" class="mw-redirect">James Sensenbrenner</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_vehicles">Military vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Military vehicles">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Military vehicles" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a>'s manned ground vehicles of the <a href="/wiki/Future_Combat_System" title="Future Combat System" class="mw-redirect">Future Combat System</a> all use a hybrid electric drive consisting of a diesel engine to generate electrical power for mobility and all other vehicle subsystems. However, with the current 2010 DOD budget all FCS land vehicles have been put on hold. Other military hybrid prototypes include the <a href="/wiki/Millenworks_Light_Utility_Vehicle" title="Millenworks Light Utility Vehicle" class="mw-redirect">Millenworks Light Utility Vehicle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_FTTS" title="International FTTS" class="mw-redirect">International FTTS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_Expanded_Mobility_Tactical_Truck" title="Heavy Expanded Mobility Tactical Truck">HEMTT model A3</a>,and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Shadow_RST-V&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Shadow RST-V (page does not exist)">Shadow RST-V</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locomotives">Locomotives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Locomotives">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Locomotives" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_Locomotive" title="Hybrid Locomotive" class="mw-redirect">Hybrid Locomotive</a></div>
<p>In May 2003, <a href="/wiki/JR_East" title="JR East" class="mw-redirect">JR East</a> started test runs with the so-called NE (new energy) train and validated the system's functionality (series hybrid with <a href="/wiki/Lithium_ion_battery" title="Lithium ion battery" class="mw-redirect">lithium ion battery</a>) in cold regions. In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Railpower_Technologies" title="Railpower Technologies">Railpower Technologies</a> had been running pilots in the US with the so-called Green Goats,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> which led to orders by the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific" title="Union Pacific" class="mw-redirect">Union Pacific</a><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific" title="Canadian Pacific" class="mw-redirect">Canadian Pacific</a><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> Railways starting in early 2005.</p>
<p>Railpower offers hybrid electric road <a href="/wiki/Switcher" title="Switcher">switchers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> as does GE.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric" title="Diesel-electric" class="mw-redirect">Diesel-electric</a> locomotives may not always be considered HEVs, not having energy storage on board, unless they are fed with electricity via a collector for short distances (for example, in tunnels with emission limits), in which case they are better classified as <a href="/wiki/Dual-mode_vehicle" title="Dual-mode vehicle">dual-mode vehicles</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_and_other_aquatic">Marine and other aquatic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Marine and other aquatic">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Marine and other aquatic" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">Electric boat</a></div>
<p>For large boats that are already diesel-electric, the upgrade to hybrid can be as straightforward as adding a large battery bank and control equipment; this configuration can provide fuel saving for the operators as well as being more environmentally sensitive.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Producers of marine hybrid propulsion include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/ECycle" title="ECycle" class="mw-redirect">eCycle</a> Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Solar_Sailor_Holdings" title="Solar Sailor Holdings">Solar Sailor Holdings</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft">Aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Aircraft">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Aircraft" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> has stated that for the subsonic concept, hybrid electric engine technology is a clear winner. Hybrid electric propulsion has the potential to shorten takeoff distance and reduce noise.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_Project_Zero" title="AgustaWestland Project Zero">AgustaWestland Project Zero</a> is one aircraft that is intented to be hybrid-electric.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hybrid_premium_and_showroom_cost_parity">Hybrid premium and showroom cost parity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Hybrid premium and showroom cost parity">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Hybrid premium and showroom cost parity" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin: 1em;">
<caption>Fuel use in vehicle designs</caption>
<tr>
<th>Vehicle type</th>
<th>Fuel used</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">All-petroleum vehicle</a></td>
<td>Most use of petroleum</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong class="selflink">Regular hybrid electric vehicle</strong></td>
<td>Less use of petroleum, but non-pluginable</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">Plug-in hybrid vehicle</a></td>
<td>Residual use of petroleum. More use of electricity</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">All-electric vehicle</a></td>
<td>Most use of electricity</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>HEVs can be initially more expensive (the so-called "hybrid premium") than pure <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil-fuel</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICE vehicles</a>, due to extra batteries, more electronics and in some cases other design considerations (although <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">battery renting can be used</a> to reach the cost parity). The <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/trade-off" class="extiw" title="wikt:trade-off">trade-off</a> between higher initial cost (also called showroom costs) and lower fuel costs (difference often referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Payback_period" title="Payback period">payback period</a>) is dependent on usage - miles traveled, or hours of operation, fuel costs, and in some cases, government subsidies. Traditional economy vehicles may result in a lower direct cost for many users (before consideration of any <a href="/wiki/Externality" title="Externality">externality</a>).</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Consumer_Reports" title="Consumer Reports">Consumer Reports</a></i> ran an article in April 2006 stating that HEVs would not pay for themselves over 5 years of ownership. However, this included an error with charging the "hybrid premium" twice.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> When corrected, the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Civic_Hybrid" title="Honda Civic Hybrid">Honda Civic Hybrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a> did have a payback period of slightly less than 5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> This includes conservative estimates with depreciation (seen as more depreciation than a conventional vehicle, although that is not the current norm) and with progressively-higher gas prices. In particular, the Consumer Reports article assumed $2/U.S.&#160;gallon for 3 years, $3/U.S.&#160;gallon for one year and $4/U.S.&#160;gallon the last year. As recent events have shown, this is a volatile market and hard to predict. For 2006, gas prices ranged from low $2 to low $3, averaging about $2.60/U.S.&#160;gallon.</p>
<p>A January 2007 analysis by Intellichoice.com shows that all 22 currently available HEVs will save their owners money over a five-year period. The most savings is for the Toyota Prius, which has a five-year cost of ownership 40.3% lower than the cost of comparable non-hybrid vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A report in the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greeley_Tribune&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Greeley Tribune (page does not exist)">Greeley Tribune</a></i> says that over the five years it would typically take for a new car owner to pay off the vehicle cost differential, a hybrid <a href="/wiki/Camry" title="Camry" class="mw-redirect">Camry</a> driver could save up to $6,700 in gasoline at current gasoline prices, with hybrid tax incentives as an additional saving.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In countries with incentives to fight against <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contamination" title="Contamination">contamination</a> and promote vehicle <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">fuel efficiency</a>, the <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pay-back" class="extiw" title="wikt:pay-back">pay-back</a> period can be immediate, and all-combustion-engine vehicles can cost more than hybrids because they generate more pollution.</p>
<p>Toyota and Honda have already said they've halved the incremental cost of electric hybrids and see cost parity in the future (even without incentives).<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Raw_materials_shortage">Raw materials shortage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Raw materials shortage">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Raw materials shortage" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle#Rare_earth_metals_availability_and_supply_security" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">Rare earth metals availability and supply security</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rare_earth_element" title="Rare earth element">rare earth element</a> <a href="/wiki/Dysprosium" title="Dysprosium">dysprosium</a> is required to fabricate many of the advanced <a href="/wiki/Electric_motors" title="Electric motors" class="mw-redirect">electric motors</a> and battery systems in hybrid propulsion systems.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cox_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cox-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>However, nearly all the <a href="/wiki/Rare_earth_elements" title="Rare earth elements" class="mw-redirect">rare earth elements</a> in the world come from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-haxel_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haxel-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> and one analyst believes that an overall increase in Chinese electronics manufacturing may consume this entire supply by 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-cox_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cox-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, export quotas on Chinese rare earth exports have resulted in a generally shaky supply of those metals.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A few non-Chinese sources such as the advanced <a href="/wiki/Hoidas_Lake" title="Hoidas Lake">Hoidas Lake</a> project in northern <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mt_Weld&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mt Weld (page does not exist)">Mt Weld</a> in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> are currently under development,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> however it is not known if these sources will be developed before a shortage hits.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation_and_incentives">Legislation and incentives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Legislation and incentives">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Legislation and incentives" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In order to encourage the purchase of HEVs, several countries have introduced legislation for <a href="/wiki/Incentive" title="Incentive">incentives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecotax" title="Ecotax">ecotaxes</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Canada">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Canada" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Residents of Ontario and Quebec in Canada can claim a rebate on the Provincial Retail Sales Tax of up to $2,000 CDN on the purchase or lease of a hybrid electric vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> Ontario has a green license plate for hybrid car users and was to announce a slew of benefits to go along with it in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> Residents in British Columbia are eligible for a 100% reduction of sales tax up to a maximum of $2,000 if the hybrid electric vehicle is purchased or leased before April 1, 2011, (extended in 2007/2008 budget from March 31, 2008, and expanded from a maximum of only $1,000 from April 1, 2008, to March 31, 2009, at which point the concession was scheduled to expire.)<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> Prince Edward Island residents can claim rebates on the Provincial Sales Tax of up to $3,000 CDN on the purchase or lease of any hybrid vehicles since March 30, 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Israel">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Israel" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Haifa,_Israel" title="Haifa, Israel" class="mw-redirect">Haifa</a>, hybrid vehicles are entitled to a free parking in city's parking lots for domestic citizens.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Japan">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Japan" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2009 the Japanese government implemented a set of policies and incentives that included a <a href="/wiki/Scrappage_program#Japan" title="Scrappage program">scrappage program</a>, tax breaks on hybrid vehicles and other low emission cars and trucks, and a higher levy on gasoline that raised prices in the order of USD 4.50 per gallon. New hybrid car sales for 2009 were almost triple those for 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday_45-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Japan_US_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_US-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jordan">Jordan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Jordan">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Jordan" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, customs and sales tax reduced for all hybrid vehicles from 55% to 25% of the vehicle list price, 12.5% customs fees and sales tax, if the new hybrid is a replacement for an old car (more than 10 years age).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Netherlands" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, the vehicle registration tax (VRT), payable when a car is sold to its first buyer, can earn the owner of an HEV a discount up to <a href="/wiki/%E2%82%AC" title="€" class="mw-redirect">€</a>6,000.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: New Zealand" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a>, hybrid vehicles are entitled to an hour free parking in city council parking buildings. Where those buildings already provide an hour free, hybrid vehicles are entitled to an extra hour free.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Ireland">Republic of Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Republic of Ireland">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Republic of Ireland" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, a discount of up to €1500 on <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_tax_(Ireland)" title="Vehicle registration tax (Ireland)">VRT</a> for hybrids, and up to €2500 for plugin hybrids is available until 31 December 2012.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.revenue.ie/en/tax/vrt/vrt-guide.html#section11">[8]</a> Previously there was a potential reduction of 50% of VRT applicable before July 2008, when VRT rates were based on engine size, rather than the current CO2 emissions system.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.cartell.ie/2010/08/lower-vrt-on-eco-friendly-cars/">[9]</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Sweden" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> there is an "Eco car" subsidy of SEK 10 000 (~ USD 1.600) cash payout to private car owners. For fringe benefit cars there is a reduction of the benefit tax of 40% for EVs &amp; HEVs and 20% for other "Eco cars".<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: United Kingdom" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Drivers of HEVs in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> benefit from the lowest band of vehicle excise duty (car tax), which is based on <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> emissions. In central <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, these vehicles are also exempt from the £8 daily <a href="/wiki/London_congestion_charge" title="London congestion charge">London congestion charge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to their low levels of regulated emissions, the greenest cars are eligible for 100% discount under the current system. To be eligible the car must be on the current Power Shift Register.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> At present, these include the cleanest <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas" title="Liquefied petroleum gas">LPG</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> cars and most hybrid-, battery- and fuel cell-electric vehicles.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: United States">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: United States" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hybrid_parking_sign_DC_07_2010_9571.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Hybrid_parking_sign_DC_07_2010_9571.JPG/200px-Hybrid_parking_sign_DC_07_2010_9571.JPG" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Hybrid_parking_sign_DC_07_2010_9571.JPG/300px-Hybrid_parking_sign_DC_07_2010_9571.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Hybrid_parking_sign_DC_07_2010_9571.JPG/400px-Hybrid_parking_sign_DC_07_2010_9571.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hybrid_parking_sign_DC_07_2010_9571.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Some <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping malls</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a> have designated reserved parking spaces for electric hybrid cars.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicles_in_the_United_States" title="Plug-in electric vehicles in the United States">Plug-in electric vehicles in the United States</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal">Federal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Federal">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Federal" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="rellink">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_tax_credit" title="Hybrid tax credit">Hybrid tax credit</a></div>
<p>The purchase of hybrid electric cars qualifies for a federal income <a href="/wiki/Tax_credit" title="Tax credit">tax credit</a> up to $3,400 on the purchaser's Federal income taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-FuelEcon_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FuelEcon-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tax_credit" title="Tax credit">tax credit</a> is to be phased out two calendar quarters after the manufacturer reaches 60,000 new cars sold in the following manner: it will be reduced to 50% if delivered in either the third or fourth quarter after the threshold is reached, to 25% in the fifth and sixth quarters, and 0% thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-IRS_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRS-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of April 2010 three auto manufactures have reached the 60,000 cap, <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Company" title="Toyota Motor Company" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Motor Company</a> reached it in 2007, <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> in 2008, and as of April 1, 2010, all <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a> hybrid vehicles are also no longer eligible for this tax credit.<sup id="cite_ref-Autotropolis_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Autotropolis-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> Vehicles purchased after December 31, 2010, are not eligible for this credit as this benefit will expire on this date.<sup id="cite_ref-FuelEcon_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FuelEcon-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Autotropolis_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Autotropolis-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="States_and_local">States and local</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: States and local">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: States and local" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>Certain states (e.g., <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>) allow singly occupied HEVs to enter the <a href="/wiki/High-occupancy_vehicle_lane" title="High-occupancy vehicle lane">HOV lanes</a> on the highway.
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:California_sticker_for_HOV_access_front_and_back_location.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/California_sticker_for_HOV_access_front_and_back_location.jpg/220px-California_sticker_for_HOV_access_front_and_back_location.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/California_sticker_for_HOV_access_front_and_back_location.jpg/330px-California_sticker_for_HOV_access_front_and_back_location.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/California_sticker_for_HOV_access_front_and_back_location.jpg/440px-California_sticker_for_HOV_access_front_and_back_location.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:California_sticker_for_HOV_access_front_and_back_location.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf12/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>'s clean air bumper sticker used to allow HEVs to access <a href="/wiki/High-occupancy_vehicle_lane" title="High-occupancy vehicle lane">HOV lanes</a>. Shown a <a href="/wiki/RechargeIT" title="RechargeIT">RechargeIT</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in</a> converted <a href="/wiki/Prius" title="Prius" class="mw-redirect">Prius</a> (left) and a conventional Toyota Prius (right).</div>
</div>
</div>
Initially, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Highway_Administration" title="Federal Highway Administration">Federal Highway Administration</a> ruled that this was a violation of federal statute<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> until August 10, 2005, when <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> signed the <a href="/wiki/Safe,_Accountable,_Flexible,_Efficient_Transportation_Equity_Act:_A_Legacy_for_Users" title="Safe, Accountable, Flexible, Efficient Transportation Equity Act: A Legacy for Users">Transportation Equity Act of 2005</a> into law. In California, a total of 85,250 owners of the three eligible hybrid models benefited from free access to HOV lanes from 2004 to mid-2011.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> This incentive expired on July 1, 2011, and now hybrids are required to comply the minimum passenger requirements to use the HOV lanes.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Some states, e.g. <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, exempt hybrid electric cars from the biennial <a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">smog</a> inspection, which costs over $50 (as of 2004<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).</li>
<li>The city of <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a> issued a free parking tag until 2007 when it became issued for a fee annually for hybrid electric cars that were purchased at a San Jose dealership. The qualified owners do not have to pay for parking in any city garage or road side parking meters.</li>
<li>The city of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" title="Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles, California</a> offers free parking to all HEVs which started on 1 October 2004. The experiment is an extension to an existing offer of free parking for all pure electrical vehicles.</li>
<li>In October 2005, the city of <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, started to offer discount on monthly parking in the city parking lots, and is considering free meter parking for HEVs. On 3 November 2005, the <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_Globe" title="Boston Globe" class="mw-redirect">Boston Globe</a></i> reports that the city council of <a href="/wiki/Boston,_Massachusetts" title="Boston, Massachusetts" class="mw-redirect">Boston</a> is considering the same treatment for hybrid electric cars.</li>
<li>Annual vehicle registration fees in the <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">District of Columbia</a> are half ($36) that paid for conventional vehicles ($72).</li>
</ul>
